<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFWilson2018">Wilson, Robinn (2018). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=345HDwAAQBAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Euler's Pioneering Equation: The most beautiful theorem in mathematics</i></a> (illustrated ed.). Oxford University Press. p. (preface). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-251405-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-251405-9"><bdi>978-0-19-251405-9</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Euler%27s+Pioneering+Equation%3A+The+most+beautiful+theorem+in+mathematics&amp;rft.pages=%28preface%29&amp;rft.edition=illustrated&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2018&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-251405-9&amp;rft.aulast=Wilson&amp;rft.aufirst=Robinn&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D345HDwAAQBAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFPosamentierLehmann2004">Posamentier, Alfred S.; Lehmann, Ingmar (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=QFPvAAAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Pi: A Biography of the World's Most Mysterious Number</i></a> (illustrated ed.). Prometheus Books. p. 68. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-59102-200-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-59102-200-8"><bdi>978-1-59102-200-8</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Pi%3A+A+Biography+of+the+World%27s+Most+Mysterious+Number&amp;rft.pages=68&amp;rft.edition=illustrated&amp;rft.pub=Prometheus+Books&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-59102-200-8&amp;rft.aulast=Posamentier&amp;rft.aufirst=Alfred+S.&amp;rft.au=Lehmann%2C+Ingmar&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DQFPvAAAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Bernoulli,_1690-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Bernoulli,_1690_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bernoulli,_1690_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Jacob Bernoulli considered the problem of continuous compounding of interest, which led to a series expression for <i>e</i>.  See:  Jacob Bernoulli (1690) "Quæstiones nonnullæ de usuris, cum solutione problematis de sorte alearum, propositi in Ephem. Gall. A. 1685" (Some questions about interest, with a solution of a problem about games of chance, proposed in the <i>Journal des Savants</i> (<i>Ephemerides Eruditorum Gallicanæ</i>), in the year (anno) 1685.**), <i>Acta eruditorum</i>, pp. 219–23.  <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=s4pw4GyHTRcC&amp;pg=PA222#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">On page 222</a>, Bernoulli poses the question:  <i>"Alterius naturæ hoc Problema est:  Quæritur, si creditor aliquis pecuniæ summam fænori exponat, ea lege, ut singulis momentis pars proportionalis usuræ annuæ sorti annumeretur; quantum ipsi finito anno debeatur?"</i>  (This is a problem of another kind:  The question is, if some lender were to invest [a] sum of money [at] interest, let it accumulate, so that [at] every moment [it] were to receive [a] proportional part of [its] annual interest; how much would he be owed [at the] end of [the] year?)  Bernoulli constructs a power series to calculate the answer, and then writes: <i>" … quæ nostra serie [mathematical expression for a geometric series] &amp;c. major est.  … si </i>a<i>=</i>b<i>, debebitur plu quam 2½</i>a<i>  &amp; minus quam 3</i>a<i>."</i> ( … which our series [a geometric series] is larger [than]. … if <i>a</i>=<i>b</i>, [the lender] will be owed more than 2½<i>a</i> and less than 3<i>a</i>.)  If <i>a</i>=<i>b</i>, the geometric series reduces to the series for <i>a</i> × <i>e</i>, so 2.5 &lt; <i>e</i> &lt; 3.  (** The reference is to a problem which Jacob Bernoulli posed and which appears in the <i>Journal des Sçavans</i> of 1685 at the bottom of <a class="external text" href="http://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k56536t/f307.image.langEN" rel="nofollow">page 314.</a>)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFCarl_BoyerUta_Merzbach1991">Carl Boyer; <a href="/wiki/Uta_Merzbach" title="Uta Merzbach">Uta Merzbach</a> (1991). <span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/historyofmathema00boye" rel="nofollow"><i>A History of Mathematics</i></a></span> (2nd ed.). Wiley. p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/historyofmathema00boye/page/419" rel="nofollow">419</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-471-54397-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-471-54397-8"><bdi>978-0-471-54397-8</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+Mathematics&amp;rft.pages=419&amp;rft.edition=2nd&amp;rft.pub=Wiley&amp;rft.date=1991&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-471-54397-8&amp;rft.au=Carl+Boyer&amp;rft.au=Uta+Merzbach&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fhistoryofmathema00boye&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFLeibniz2003">Leibniz, Gottfried Wilhelm (2003). <a class="external text" href="https://leibniz.uni-goettingen.de/files/pdf/Leibniz-Edition-III-5.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Sämliche Schriften Und Briefe"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (in German). <q>look for example letter nr. 6</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=S%C3%A4mliche+Schriften+Und+Briefe&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.aulast=Leibniz&amp;rft.aufirst=Gottfried+Wilhelm&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fleibniz.uni-goettingen.de%2Ffiles%2Fpdf%2FLeibniz-Edition-III-5.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lettre XV.  Euler à Goldbach, dated November 25, 1731 in:  P.H. Fuss, ed., <i>Correspondance Mathématique et Physique de Quelques Célèbres Géomètres du XVIIIeme Siècle</i> … (Mathematical and physical correspondence of some famous geometers of the 18th century), vol. 1, (St. Petersburg, Russia:  1843), pp. 56–60, see especially <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gf1OEXIQQgsC&amp;pg=PA58#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">p. 58.</a>  From p. 58:  <i>" … ( e denotat hic numerum, cujus logarithmus hyperbolicus est = 1), … "</i> ( … (e denotes that number whose hyperbolic [i.e., natural] logarithm is equal to 1) … )</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRemmert1991"><a href="/wiki/Reinhold_Remmert" title="Reinhold Remmert">Remmert, Reinhold</a> (1991). <i>Theory of Complex Functions</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springer-Verlag" title="Springer-Verlag">Springer-Verlag</a>. p. 136. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-387-97195-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-387-97195-7"><bdi>978-0-387-97195-7</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Theory+of+Complex+Functions&amp;rft.pages=136&amp;rft.pub=Springer-Verlag&amp;rft.date=1991&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-387-97195-7&amp;rft.aulast=Remmert&amp;rft.aufirst=Reinhold&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Meditatio-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Meditatio_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Euler, <i><a class="external text" href="https://scholarlycommons.pacific.edu/euler-works/853/" rel="nofollow">Meditatio in experimenta explosione tormentorum nuper instituta</a></i>. <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Scribatur pro numero cujus logarithmus est unitas, e, qui est 2,7182817…</i></span> (English: Written for the number of which the logarithm has the unit, e, that is 2,7182817...")</span>

<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSteven_Finch2003">Steven Finch (2003). <span class="cs1-lock-registration" title="Free registration required"><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/mathematicalcons0000finc" rel="nofollow"><i>Mathematical constants</i></a></span>. <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is the approach taken by Kline (1998).</span>

(2006). <a class="external text" href="http://www.maa.org/sites/default/files/pdf/upload_library/22/Chauvenet/mccartin.pdf" rel="nofollow">"e: The Master of All"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>The Mathematical Intelligencer</i>. <b>28</b> (2): 10–21. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1007%2Fbf02987150" rel="nofollow">10.1007/bf02987150</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:123033482" rel="nofollow">123033482</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Mathematical+Intelligencer&amp;rft.atitle=e%3A+The+Master+of+All&amp;rft.volume=28&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=10-21&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1007%2Fbf02987150&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A123033482%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.au=McCartin%2C+Brian+J.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.maa.org%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fpdf%2Fupload_library%2F22%2FChauvenet%2Fmccartin.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AE+%28mathematical+constant%29"></span></li></ul>
